window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Muse_(band)';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"band,muse,(,_,),";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Muse</b>
are
an
English
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
from
<a
href="/wiki/Teignmouth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teignmouth">Teignmouth</a>,
Devon,
formed
in
1994.
The
band
consists
of
school
friends
<a
href="/wiki/Matthew_Bellamy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matthew
Bellamy">Matthew
Bellamy</a>
(lead
vocals,
lead
guitar,
piano,
keyboards,
<a
href="/wiki/Keytar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keytar">keytar</a>),
<a
href="/wiki/Christopher_Wolstenholme?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christopher
Wolstenholme">Christopher
Wolstenholme</a>
(bass,
vocals,
keyboards)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Dominic_Howard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dominic
Howard">Dominic
Howard</a>
(drums,
percussion,
synthesisers).</p>








<p>Since
the
release
of
their
2006
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Black_Holes_and_Revelations?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Holes
and
Revelations">Black
Holes
and
Revelations</a></i>,
keyboardist
and
percussionist
<a
href="/wiki/Morgan_Nicholls?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Morgan
Nicholls">Morgan
Nicholls</a>
has
performed
live
with
the
band.
Muse
are
known
for
their
energetic
and
extravagant
live
performances<sup
id="cite_ref-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup

and
their
fusion
of
many
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
genre">music
genres</a>,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Space_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Space

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Progressive
rock">progressive

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative

nominated
for
five
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
of
which
they
won
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album">Best
Rock
Album</a>,
for
their
fifth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
(album)">The
Resistance</a></i>
(2009).<sup
id="cite_ref-gawrd_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gawrd-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
To
date,
Muse
have
sold
over
15
million
albums
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1994.E2.80.931998:_Formation_and_early_years">1994â€“1998:
Formation
and
early
years</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
1994â€“1998:
Formation
and
early
years">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
members
of
Muse
played
in
separate
school
bands
during
their
stay
at
<a
href="/wiki/Teignmouth_Community_College?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teignmouth
Community
College"
class="mw-redirect">Teignmouth
Community
College</a>
in
the
early
1990s,
but
the
formation
of
Muse
began
when
Bellamy
successfully
auditioned
for
the
part
of
guitarist
in
Dominic
Howard's
band,
Carnage
Mayhem.
They
asked
Chris
Wolstenholme
â€“
who
played
the
drums
at
the
time
â€“
to
learn
to
play
bass
guitar
for
the
band,
Wolstenholme
agreed
and
took
up
lessons,
while
Bellamy
had
to
become
singer
and
songwriter
for
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
other
original
band
members
left
after
Bellamy
suggested
that
they
write
their
own
songs
rather
than
doing
covers.</p>








<p>Bellamy
and
Howard's
first
band
name
was
Gothic
Plague.
They
later
changed
the
name
to
Fixed
Penalty
and
then
to
Rocket
Baby
Dolls.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1994
the
band
used
the
name
Rocket
Baby
Dolls<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
a
goth/glam
image
to
compete
in
a
local
<a
href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_bands?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Battle
of
the
bands"
class="mw-redirect">battle
of
the
bands</a>.
The
band
won
the
contest,
smashing
their
equipment
in
the
process.<sup
id="cite_ref-MicrocutsBio_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MicrocutsBio-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-KerrangReview_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KerrangReview-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;It
was
supposed
to
be
a
protest,
a
statement&quot;,
Bellamy
said,
&quot;so,
when
we
actually
won,
it
was
a
real
shock,
a
massive
shock.
After
that,
we
started
taking
ourselves
seriously.&quot;
Shortly
after
the
contest,
the
three
decided
to
forget
university,
quit
their
jobs,
change
the
band
name
to
Muse
(1994â€“1995),
and
move
away
from
Teignmouth.<sup
id="cite_ref-TasteBio_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TasteBio-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
name
&quot;Muse&quot;
was
supposedly
inspired
by
Matthew
Bellamy's
art
teacher
Samuel
Theoun.
The
band
liked
that
it
was
short
and
thought
that
it
looked
good
on
a
poster.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Music
journalist
Mark
Beaumont
writes
in
his
biography
of
the
band,
that
they
wanted
the
name
to
reflect
&quot;the
sense
Matt
had
that
he
had
somehow
'summoned
up'
this
band,
the
way
mediums
could
summon
up
inspirational
spirits
at
times
of
emotional
need.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1998.E2.80.932000:_First_EPs_and_Showbiz">1998â€“2000:
First
EPs
and
<i>Showbiz</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1998â€“2000:
First
EPs
and
Showbiz">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Showbiz_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Showbiz
(album)">Showbiz
(album)</a>







</div>








<p>After
a
few
years
building
a
fan
base,
Muse
played
their
first
gigs
in
London
and
<a
href="/wiki/Manchester?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manchester">Manchester</a>
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/Skunk_Anansie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skunk
Anansie">Skunk
Anansie</a>
on
tour.
The
band
had
a
significant
meeting
with
Dennis
Smith,
the
owner
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sawmills_Studio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sawmills
Studio">Sawmills
Studio</a>,
situated
in
a
converted
water
mill
in
<a
href="/wiki/Cornwall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.
He
had
seen
the
three
boys
grow
up
as
he
knew
their
parents
and
had
a
production
company
together
with
their
future
manager
<a
href="/wiki/Safta_Jaffery?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Safta
Jaffery">Safta
Jaffery</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:202px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Muse_logo.svg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Muse_logo.svg/200px-Muse_logo.svg.png"
width="200"
height="84"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Muse_logo.svg/300px-Muse_logo.svg.png

http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Muse_logo.svg/400px-Muse_logo.svg.png
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Muse_logo.svg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
The
Muse
logo,
incorporated
chiefly
since
the
release
of











<a
href="/wiki/Muse_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muse
(EP)"><i>Muse</i>
EP</a>
in
1998









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>This
meeting
led
to
their
first
proper
recordings
and
the
release
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Muse_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muse
(EP)"><i>Muse</i>
EP</a>
on
11
May
1998
on
Sawmills'
in-house
<a
href="/wiki/Dangerous_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dangerous
Records"
class="mw-redirect">Dangerous</a>
label.<sup
id="cite_ref-MicrocutsBio_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MicrocutsBio-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
second
EP,
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Muscle_Museum_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muscle
Museum
EP">Muscle
Museum
EP</a></i>
released
on
11
January
1999,
reached
number
3
in
the
indie
singles
chart
and
attracted
the
attention
of
British
radio
broadcaster
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Lamacq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Lamacq">Steve
Lamacq</a>
as
well
as
the
weekly
British
music
publication
<i>NME</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Muse_-_Fuse.tv_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Muse_-_Fuse.tv-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dennis
Smith
introduced
the
band
to
<a
href="/wiki/Safta_Jaffery?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Safta
Jaffery">Safta
Jaffery</a>,
with
whom
he
had
recently
started
the
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Taste_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taste
Media">Taste
Media</a>.
Later
in
1999,
Muse
performed
on
the
Emerging
Artist's
stage
at
Woodstock
1999.
Muse
signed
with
Smith
and
Jaffery
and
recorded
their
first
three
albums:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Showbiz_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Showbiz
(album)">Showbiz</a></i>
(1999),
<i><a
href="/wiki/Origin_of_Symmetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Origin
of
Symmetry">Origin
of
Symmetry</a></i>
(2001),
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Absolution_(Muse_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolution
(Muse
album)"
class="mw-redirect">Absolution</a></i>
(2003),
with
<a
href="/wiki/Taste_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taste
Media">Taste
Media</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Muse_-_Fuse.tv_19-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Muse_-_Fuse.tv-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Despite
the
success
of
their
second
EP,
British
record
companies
were
reluctant
to
sign
Muse.
After
a
trip
to
New
York's
CMJ
Festival
Nanci
Walker,
then
Sr.
Director
of
A&amp;R
at
Columbia
Records,
flew
Muse
to
the
US
to
showcase
for
Columbia
Records'
then-Senior
Vice-President
of
A&amp;R,
Tim
Devine,
as
well
as
for
American
Recording's
Rick
Rubin.
During
this
trip,
on
24
December
1998,
Muse
signed
a
deal
with
American
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Maverick_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maverick
Records">Maverick
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
Upon
their
return
from
America,
Taste
Media
arranged
deals
for
Muse
with
various
record
labels
in
Europe
and
Australia,
allowing
them
to
maintain
control
over
their
career
in
individual
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/John_Leckie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Leckie">John
Leckie</a>
was
brought
in
alongside
the
MUSE
and
Muscle
Museum
EP
producer,
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Reeve?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Reeve">Paul
Reeve</a>,
to
co
produce
the
band's
first
record,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Showbiz_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Showbiz
(album)">Showbiz</a></i>
(1999).
The
album
effectively
showcased
Muse's
aggressive
yet
melancholic
musical
style.
Lyrics
in
the
songs
referenced
human
relationships
and
difficulties
they
had
encountered
while
trying
to
establish
themselves
in
their
hometown.<sup
id="cite_ref-MicrocutsBio_13-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MicrocutsBio-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-KerrangReview_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KerrangReview-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2001.E2.80.932002:_Origin_of_Symmetry_and_Hullabaloo">2001â€“2002:
<i>Origin
of
Symmetry</i>
and
<i>Hullabaloo</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
2001â€“2002:
Origin
of
Symmetry
and
Hullabaloo">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Origin_of_Symmetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Origin
of
Symmetry">Origin
of
Symmetry</a>







</div>








<p>During
production
of
the
band's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Origin_of_Symmetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Origin
of
Symmetry">Origin
of
Symmetry</a></i>
(2001),
the
band
experimented
with
instrumentation
such
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Church_organ?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Church
organ"
class="mw-redirect">church
organ</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Mellotron?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mellotron">Mellotron</a>,
animal
bones,
and
an
expanded
drum
kit.
There
were
more
of
Bellamy's
high-pitched
vocal
lines,
<a
href="/wiki/Arpeggio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arpeggio">arpeggiated</a>
guitar,
and
piano
playing.
Bellamy
cites
guitar
influences
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimi
Hendrix">Jimi
Hendrix</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Morello?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Morello">Tom
Morello</a>
(of
<a
href="/wiki/Rage_Against_the_Machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rage
Against
the
Machine">Rage
Against
the
Machine</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Audioslave?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Audioslave">Audioslave</a>),
the
latter
evident
in
the
more
<a
href="/wiki/Riff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Riff"
class="mw-redirect">riff</a>-based
songs
in
<i>Origin
of
Symmetry</i>
and
in
Bellamy's
extensive
use
of
pitch-shifting
effects
in
his
solos.<sup
id="cite_ref-bellamy_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bellamy-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
features
a
reworking
of
<a
href="/wiki/Anthony_Newley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anthony
Newley">Anthony
Newley</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Leslie_Bricusse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leslie
Bricusse">Leslie
Bricusse</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Feeling_Good?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Feeling
Good">Feeling
Good</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
track
was
later
used
as
the
backing
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Virgin_Airways?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virgin
Airways"
class="mw-redirect">Virgin
Airways</a>
UK
TV
advertisement.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2002,
Muse
threatened
<a
href="/wiki/Celine_Dion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Celine
Dion">Celine
Dion</a>
with
legal
action,
when
she
planned
to
name
her
<a
href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Las
Vegas
Strip">Las
Vegas</a>
show
as
&quot;Muse&quot;,
despite
the
band
owning
the
worldwide
performing
rights
to
the
name.
Dion
offered
Muse
$50,000
for
the
rights,
but
they
turned
it
down.
Bellamy
later
stated,
that
&quot;We
don't
want
to
turn
up
there
with
people
thinking
we're
Celine
Dion's
backing
band.&quot;
Eventually
Dion
was
forced
to
back
down.<sup
id="cite_ref-celine_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-celine-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Origin
of
Symmetry</i>
(2001)
was
well
received
by
critics;
NME
gave
the
album
9/10
with
Roger
Morton
writing:
&quot;It's
amazing
for
such
a
young
band
to
load
up
with
a
heritage
that
includes
the
darker
visions
of
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Cobain</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Kafka?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kafka"
class="mw-redirect">Kafka</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Mahler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mahler"
class="mw-redirect">Mahler</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Tiger_Lillies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Tiger
Lillies">The
Tiger
Lillies</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/David_Cronenberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Cronenberg">Cronenberg</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Arnold_Schoenberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arnold
Schoenberg">Schoenberg</a>,
and
make
a
sexy,
populist
album.
But
Muse
have
carried
it
off.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Maverick
had
reservations
about
Bellamy's
vocal
style
on
this
album
(considering
it
not
to
be
&quot;radio-friendly&quot;)
and
asked
Muse
to
change
some
of
their
songs
prior
to
US
release.
The
band
refused
and
left
Maverick,
resulting
in
Maverick's
decision
not
to
release
<i>Origin
of
Symmetry</i>
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-SPI_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SPI-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
finally
released
in
the
US
in
September
2005,
after
Muse
signed
to
Warner
Bros.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Muse
released
a
live
DVD,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hullabaloo_Soundtrack?qsrc=3044#DVD"
title="Hullabaloo
Soundtrack">Hullabaloo</a></i>,
featuring
live
footage
recorded
during
Muse's
two
gigs
on
consecutive
nights
at
<a
href="/wiki/Le_Zenith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Le
Zenith"
class="mw-redirect">Le
Zenith</a>
in
Paris
in
2001
and
a
documentary
film
of
the
band
on
tour.
A
double
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hullabaloo_Soundtrack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hullabaloo
Soundtrack">Hullabaloo
Soundtrack</a></i>,
was
released
at
the
same
time,
containing
a
compilation
of
<a
href="/wiki/B-side?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B-side"
class="mw-redirect">B-sides</a>
and
a
disc
of
recordings
of
songs
from
the
Le
Zenith
performances.
A
double-A
side
single
was
also
released
featuring
new
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_Your_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Your
World"
class="mw-redirect">In
Your
World</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dead_Star/In_Your_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dead
Star/In
Your
World">Dead
Star</a>&quot;.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2003.E2.80.932005:_Absolution">2003â€“2005:
<i>Absolution</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
2003â€“2005:
Absolution">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink

mainarticle">

article:









<a

(Muse
album)"

(Muse
album)</a>







</div>

</div>
Chris
Wolstenholme
of
Muse
performing
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/Mod_Club_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mod
Club
Theatre">Mod
Club
Theatre</a>,
Toronto
in
2004.
The
international











<i>Absolution</i>
tour
included
the
band's
first
shows
in
North
America
since
1999.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Absolution_(Muse_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolution
(Muse
album)"
class="mw-redirect">Absolution</a></i>
(produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Rich_Costey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rich
Costey">Rich
Costey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Reeve?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Reeve">Paul
Reeve</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/John_Cornfield?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Cornfield">John
Cornfield</a>)
was
released
in
September
2003
and
debuted
at
number
one
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
yielded
their
first
top
ten
hit
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Time_Is_Running_Out_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Time
Is
Running
Out
(Muse
song)">Time
Is
Running
Out</a>&quot;
and
later
three
top-twenty
hits:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hysteria_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hysteria
(Muse
song)">Hysteria</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sing_for_Absolution?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sing
for
Absolution">Sing
for
Absolution</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Butterflies_and_Hurricanes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butterflies
and
Hurricanes">Butterflies
and
Hurricanes</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>Muse
subsequently
undertook
an
international
tour
in
support
of
the
album.
It
continued
for
about
a
year
and
saw
Muse
visiting
Australia,
New
Zealand,
the
United
States,
Canada,
and
France.
Meanwhile,
the
band
released
six
singles
(one
being
for
charity)
(&quot;Time
Is
Running
Out&quot;,
&quot;Hysteria&quot;,
&quot;Sing
for
Absolution&quot;,
Falling
Away
With
You,
Endlessly,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stockholm_Syndrome_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stockholm
Syndrome
(song)">Stockholm
Syndrome</a>&quot;,
&quot;Butterflies
and
Hurricanes&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Apocalypse_Please?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apocalypse
Please">Apocalypse
Please</a>&quot;).
The
US
leg
of
the
2004
tour
began
ominously
as
Bellamy
injured
himself
on
stage
during
the
opening
show
in
Atlanta.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
resumed
after
Bellamy
got
several
stitches
and
had
a
couple
of
days
of
rest.</p>








<p>The
band
also
played
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury
Festival</a>
in
June
2004.
After
the
festival,
the
band
described
the
concert
as
&quot;the
best
gig
of
our
lives&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
Drummer
Dominic
Howard's
father,
William
Howard,
who
attended
the
festival
to
watch
the
band,
died
from
a
heart
attack
shortly
after
the
performance.
&quot;It
was
the
biggest
feeling
of
achievement
we've
ever
had
after
coming
offstage&quot;,
Bellamy
said.
&quot;It
was
almost
surreal
that
an
hour
later
his
dad
died.
It
was
almost
not
believable.
We
spent
about
a
week
sort
of
just
with
Dom
trying
to
support
him.
I
think
he
was
happy
that
at
least
his
dad
got
to
see
him
at
probably
what
was
the
finest
moment
so
far
of
the
band's
life&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-MicrocutsBio_13-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MicrocutsBio-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Muse
then
continued
their
tour.
They
won
2
MTV
Europe
awards,
including
&quot;Best
Alternative
Act&quot;
and
a
Q
Award
for
&quot;Best
Live
Act&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-MSE_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MSE-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Muse
also
received
an
award
for
&quot;Best
British
Live
Act&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/BRIT_Awards?qsrc=3044#2005_awards"
title="BRIT
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Brit
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MSE_34-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MSE-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
July
2005,
Muse
participated
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Live_8?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
8">Live
8</a>
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Live_8_concert,_Paris?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
8
concert,
Paris">Paris</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2003,
the
band
sued
<a
href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nestl&eacute;">Nestl&eacute;</a>,
who
used
their
cover
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hyper_Music/Feeling_Good?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyper
Music/Feeling
Good">Feeling
Good</a>&quot;
for
a
Nescaf&eacute;
advertisement
without
the
band's
permission.
The
group
donated
the
money
won
from
the
suit
to
<a
href="/wiki/Oxfam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>.
A
driving
force
behind
the
legal
action
was
Muse
bassist
Christopher
Wolstenholme,
who
had
recently
had
his
third
child
and
was
critical
of
Nestl&eacute;
for
promoting
powdered
milk
to
new
mothers
in
developing
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>An
unofficial
and
unauthorised
DVD
biography
containing
no
Muse
music
called
<i>Manic
Depression</i>
was
released
in
April
2005;
the
band
was
not
involved
with
the
project
and
did
not
endorse
the
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Another
DVD,
this
time
official,
was
released
by
the
band
on
12
December
2005,
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Absolution_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolution
Tour">Absolution
Tour</a></i>.
The
official
release
contained
re-edited
and
re-mastered
highlights
from
the
Glastonbury
Festival
2004
and
previously
unseen
footage
from
London
Earls
Court,
Wembley
Arena,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wiltern_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wiltern
Theatre"
class="mw-redirect">Wiltern
Theatre</a>
in
Los
Angeles.
Two
songs,
&quot;Endlessly&quot;
and
&quot;Thoughts
of
a
Dying
Atheist&quot;,
are
hidden
tracks
on
the
DVD
taken
from
Wembley
Arena.
The
only
song
from
<i>Absolution</i>
not
to
appear
on
the
live
DVD
is
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Falling_Away_With_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Falling
Away
With
You"
class="mw-redirect">Falling
Away
With
You</a>&quot;.
<i>Absolution</i>
eventually
went
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">Gold</a>
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="mw-headline"

<a

title="Starlight

at

<p>In
2006,
Muse
released
their
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Black_Holes_and_Revelations?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Holes
and
Revelations">Black
Holes
and
Revelations</a></i>,
co-produced
by
Muse
and
Rich
Costey.
The
album's
title
and
themes
are
the
result
of
the
band's
fascination
with
science
fiction
and
political
outrage.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
album
charted
at
No.&nbsp;1
in
the
UK,
much
of
Europe,
and
Australia.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
also
a
success
in
the
United
States,
reaching
number
nine
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Prior
to
the
release
of
the
new
album,
the
band
resumed
making
live
performances,
which
had
halted
while
recording,
making
a
number
of
promotional
TV
appearances
starting
on
13
May
2006
at
<a
href="/wiki/BBC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC">BBC</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_1%27s_Big_Weekend?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
1's
Big
Weekend">Radio
1's
Big
Weekend</a>.
The
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Holes_and_Revelations_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Holes
and
Revelations
Tour">Black
Holes
and
Revelations
Tour</a>
started
just
before
the
release
of
their
album
and
initially
consisted
mostly
of
festival
appearances,
most
notably
a
headline
slot
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festivals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
and
Leeds
Festivals">Reading
and
Leeds
Festivals</a>
in
August
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
main
touring
itinerary
started
with
a
tour
of
North
America
from
late
July
to
early
August
2006.
After
the
last
of
the
summer
festivals,
a
tour
of
Europe
began,
including
a
large
arena
tour
of
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>Black
Holes
and
Revelations</i>
was
nominated
for
the
2006
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Music
Prize"
class="mw-redirect">Mercury
Music
Prize</a>,
but
lost
to
<a
href="/wiki/Arctic_Monkeys?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arctic
Monkeys">Arctic
Monkeys</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
did,
however,
earn
a
<a
href="/wiki/Platinum_Europe_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Platinum
Europe
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Platinum
Europe
Award</a>
after
selling
one
million
copies
in
the
continent.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Supermassive_Black_Hole_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supermassive
Black
Hole
(song)">Supermassive
Black
Hole</a>&quot;,
was
released
as
a
download
in
May
2006.
It
was
later
followed
by
general
releases
as
a
single
the
next
month,
all
ahead
of
the
main
album
release.
In
August
2006,
Muse
recorded
a
live
session
at
<a
href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Abbey
Road
Studios">Abbey
Road
Studios</a>
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_from_Abbey_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
from
Abbey
Road">Live
from
Abbey
Road</a></i>.</p>








<p>The
second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Starlight_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Starlight
(Muse
song)">Starlight</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
September
2006.
&quot;<a

title="Knights
of
Cydonia">Knights
of
Cydonia</a>&quot;
was
released
in

in

2006
and
in
the
UK
in
November
2006.
&quot;Knights
of
Cydonia&quot;
was
voted
number
1
in
the
world's
largest
music
poll
Australian
Radio's
<a
href="/wiki/Triple_J_Hottest_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Triple
J
Hottest
100">Triple
J
Hottest
100</a>
for
2007
and
18th
in
Triple
J's
Hottest
100
of
All
Time
in
2009.
The
fourth
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Invincible_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Invincible
(Muse
song)">Invincible</a>&quot;,
was
then
released
in

2007.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
Another
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Map_of_the_Problematique?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Map
of
the
Problematique">Map
of

Problematique</a>&quot;,
was

for

only

at

id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a

<p>The
band
spent
November
and
much
of
December
2006
touring
Europe
with
British
band
<a
href="/wiki/Noisettes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Noisettes">Noisettes</a>
as
the
supporting
act.
The
tour
continued
in
Australia,
New
Zealand,
and
Southeast
Asia
in
early
2007
before
returning
to
England
for
the
summer.
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/2007_BRIT_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2007
BRIT
Awards">2007</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>
in
February,
Muse
received
their
second
award
for
Best
British
Live
Act.<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Possibly
their
biggest
performances
to
date
were
two
gigs
at
the
newly
rebuilt
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium">Wembley
Stadium</a>
on
16
and
17
June
2007,
which
they
opened
using
the
piece
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Montagues_and_Capulets?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montagues
and
Capulets">Montagues
and
Capulets</a>&quot;,
which
is
titled
as
&quot;Intro&quot;
on
the
album's
back.
Both
Wembley
concerts
were
recorded
for
a
DVD/CD
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/HAARP_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="HAARP
(album)">HAARP</a></i>,
which
was
released
on
17
March
2008<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
in
the
UK
and
1
April
2008<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
in
the
US.
It
was
named
the
40th
greatest
live
album
of
all
time
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Wembley_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Wembley-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
touring
continued
across
Europe
in
July
2007
before
heading
back
to
the
US
in
August,
where
they
played
to
a
sold
out
crowd
at
<a

<a

<a

Not

<a

<a

<p>Muse

Muse
performing
&quot;










<a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
(album)">Resistance</a>&quot;
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/National_Indoor_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Indoor
Arena">National
Indoor
Arena</a>,
Birmingham
on
10
November
2009.









</div>

<p>The
band's
fifth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
(album)">The
Resistance</a></i>
was
released
in
September
2009.
It
is
the
first
Muse
album
to
have
been
produced
by
the
band
itself.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
engineered
by
Adrian
Bushby
and
mixed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Stent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Stent"
class="mw-redirect">Mark
Stent</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
its
release,
it
topped
the
album
charts
in
19
countries,
became
the
band's
third
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Album_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Album
Chart"
class="mw-redirect">number
one
album</a>
in
the
UK,<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
reached
number
three
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Critics
were
mostly
positive
about
the
album,
with
much
of
the
praise
directed
towards
its
ambition,
classical
music
influences
and
the
thirteen-minute,
three-part
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Exogenesis:_Symphony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Exogenesis:
Symphony">Exogenesis:
Symphony</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
also
beat
its
predecessor
<i>Black
Holes
and
Revelations</i>
in
relative
album
sales
in
its
debut
week
in
the
UK
with
approximately
148,000
copies
sold.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Uprising_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uprising
(song)">Uprising</a>&quot;,
was
released
seven
days
earlier.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
13
September,
Muse
performed
&quot;Uprising&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2009
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">2009
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
in
New
York
City.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
Tour">The
Resistance
Tour</a>
started
with
a
Seaside
Rendezvous
in
<a
href="/wiki/Teignmouth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teignmouth">Teignmouth</a>,
Devon
in
September
2009
and
included
headlining
Coachella
Festival
in
April
2010.
It
also
included
two
gigs
at
Wembley
Stadium
in
September
2010.
The
band
also
supported
the
<a
href="/wiki/U2_360%C2%B0_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2
360&deg;
Tour">U2
360&deg;
Tour</a>.
In
the
&quot;Breakfast
with
Muse
Concert&quot;
<a
href="/wiki/KROQ-FM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KROQ-FM">KROQ-FM</a>
held,
Muse
was
asked,
how
long
they
would
be
on
tour.
They
commented
saying
in
a
paraphrase:
&quot;We
will
probably
be
touring
until
the
end
of
next
year.
We
will
be
doing
this
U2
and
European
tour
and
ship
off
to
Australia
and
Asia
and
return
for
an
extensive
US
tour.
It
will
actually
be
our
longest
US
tour
to
date.
Starting
at
about
the
end
of
February
or
March.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
January
2010,
Muse
headlined
the
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Day_Out?qsrc=3044"

in

<a

with
<a

headlined
Coachella
on

<p>On
20
April
2010,
the
band
announced
fourteen
dates
for
a
North
American
tour,
which
were
to
be
held
between
September
and
November
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition
to
this,
the
band
had
added
further
four
dates
to
their
forthcoming
North
American
tour,
on
28
April
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
7
May
2010,
it
was
announced,
that
Muse
would
provide
a
pre-written
song
to
be
the
lead
single
for
the
third
film
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga:_Eclipse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse">The
Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse</a></i>.
The
<a
href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga:_Eclipse_(soundtrack)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse
(soundtrack)">soundtrack</a>'s
lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Neutron_Star_Collision_(Love_Is_Forever)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neutron
Star
Collision
(Love
Is
Forever)">Neutron
Star
Collision
(Love
Is
Forever)</a>&quot;
was
released
on
17
May
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
the
band's
third
appearance
in
the
soundtrack
of
a
<a
href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga_(film_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Twilight
Saga
(film
series)"><i>Twilight</i>
film</a>.</p>








<p>Muse
played
at
<a
href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glastonbury
Festival">Glastonbury</a>
in
June
2010
and
were
joined
onstage
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Edge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Edge">The
Edge</a>
from
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
to
play
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Where_the_Streets_Have_No_Name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Where
the
Streets
Have
No
Name">Where
the
Streets
Have
No
Name</a>&quot;,
after
U2
pulled
out
of
their
headlining
slot
due
to
lead
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Bono?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bono">Bono</a>'s
back
injury.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Muse's
fearsome
live
reputation
helped
secure
them
the
O2
<a
href="/wiki/Silver_Clef_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silver
Clef
Award">Silver
Clef
Award</a>
in
London
on
2
July
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
award
was
presented
by
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows_Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Meddows
Taylor">Roger
Taylor</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_May?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
May">Brian
May</a>.
Taylor
described
the
trio
as
&quot;probably
the
greatest
live
act
in
the
world
today&quot;,
while
May
said
that
&quot;this
is
a
magnificent,
incredible
group.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On
12
September
2010,
Muse
won
a
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award">MTV
Video
Music
Award</a>
in
the
category
of
Best
Special
Effects,
for
the
&quot;Uprising&quot;
promo.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
21
November,
Muse
took
home
an
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Award">American
Music
Award</a>
for
Favorite
Artist
in
the
Alternative
Rock
Music
Category.<sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
2
December,
Muse
were
nominated
for
three
awards
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/53rd_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="53rd
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">53rd
Grammy
Awards</a>
on
13
February
2011,
for
which
they
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album</a>
for
<i>The
Resistance</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-gawrd_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gawrd-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Based
on
having
the
largest
airplay
and
sales
in
the
US,
Muse
were
named
the
<i>Billboard</i>
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
Songs">Alternative
Songs</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
Songs"
class="mw-redirect">Rock
Songs</a>
artist
for
2010
with
&quot;Uprising&quot;,
&quot;Resistance&quot;
and
&quot;Undisclosed
Desires&quot;
achieving
1st,
6th
and
49th
on
the
year
end
Alternative
Song
chart
respectively.<sup
id="cite_ref-87"

<p>In

had
begun

to

by

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>

as

gangsta

ambient

and

on

account.<sup

href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In

that
the
band
were
set
to

of
<a

from

such
as
<a

<a

(band)">Justice</a>

<a

Rock"
class="mw-redirect">Electronic

group
<a

<p>Muse
revealed
<i>The
2nd
Law</i>
tracklist
on
13

in

official

id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-105"

href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
second
single
from
<i>The
2nd
Law</i>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Madness_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

(Muse
song)">Madness</a>&quot;,
was
released
on
20
August
2012,
and

music
video
for
the
song
came
out
on
5

Muse
played
at
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Roundhouse"

on
30
September
to
promote
their
new
album
as

of

<a
href="/wiki/ITunes_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes
Festival">iTunes
Festival</a>.
<i>The
2nd
Law</i>
was
released
worldwide
on
1
October,
and
on
2
October
2012
in
the
United
States;
the
album
subsequently
reached
number
one
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">UK
Albums
Chart</a>,
and
number
two
on
the
US
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Madness_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madness
(Muse
song)">Madness</a>&quot;
earned
a
nomination
in

<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Song?qsrc=3044"

title="Best

class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Song</a>
category
and
the
album
itself
was

for

<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/55th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"

title="55th
Grammy
Awards"

Awards</a>,
2013.
The
band
performed
the

&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Supremacy_(song)?qsrc=3044"

(song)">Supremacy</a>&quot;,
with
a

at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2013_BRIT_Awards?qsrc=3044"

title="2013
BRIT
Awards">2013

Awards</a>
on
20
February
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
instrumental
versions
of
two
songs
from
the
album,
The
2nd
Law:
Isolated
System
and
<a
href="/wiki/Follow_Me_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"

(Muse

were

in

in

2013

<i><a
href="/wiki/World_War_Z_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World

Z
(film)">World

Z</a></i>.
Leading

<a

Pitt">Brad
