in
an
interview
that
he
was
in
search
of
a
song
that
could
be
associated
with
the
film
like
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Oldfield?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Oldfield">Mike
Oldfield</a>'s
iconic
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tubular_Bells?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tubular
Bells">Tubular
Bells</a></i>
is
connected
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Exorcist_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Exorcist
(film)">The
Exorcist</a></i>.
Pitt
thought
the
songs
were
&quot;exactly
what
we
were
looking
for
for
the
film&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-110"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
has
released
their
third
live
album:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_at_Rome_Olympic_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
at
Rome
Olympic
Stadium">Live
at
Rome
Olympic
Stadium</a></i>,
from
29
November
2013
in
the
CD/DVD
and
CD/Blu-ray
formats.
On
5
November
2013,
the
film
will
also
get
theatrical
screenings
in
20
cities
worldwide,
in
the
U.S.
and
Canada
on
6
November
2013,
in
Europe,
UK,
Australia
and
Japan
on
7
November
2013,
on
12
November
2013
in
Austria,
Germany,
Italy
and
Spain,
on
19
November
2013
in
Poland,
and
22-24
November
2013
in
Indonesia.
This
is
the
first
concert
filmed
in
<a
href="/wiki/4K_resolution?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="4K
resolution">4K</a>
format.
The
album
contains
the
band's
performance
at
<a
href="/wiki/Rome?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rome">Rome</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stadio
Olimpico">Stadio
Olimpico</a>
on
6
July
2013,
in
front
of
a
crowd
of
60,963
people.
The
concert
was
a
part
of
The
Unsustainable
Tour,
which
is
a
moniker
for
the
band's
summer
2013
European
leg
of
The
2nd
Law
World
Tour.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2014.E2.80.93:_Seventh_studio_album">2014â€“:
<i>Seventh
studio
album</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
2014â€“:
Seventh
studio
album">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>During
a
gig
in
<a
href="/wiki/Helsinki?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>,
the
band
performed
two
songs
from
their
1990's
B-Side
library
that
had
not
been
played
in
recent
years:
&quot;Agitated&quot;
and
&quot;Yes
Please&quot;.
Both
songs
were
not
on
the
original
set-list
for
the
gig.
Following
the
gig,
Bellamy
said:
&quot;We
haven't
played
those
songs
in
like
6
years...
Something
like
that.
That
was
a
rehearsal.
That's
what
the
next
album
sounds
like,
okay?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-111"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
stated
how
the
band
plans
to
return
to
the
studio
in
2014
after
a
short
break.</p>








<p>On
November
25,
2013,
Bellamy
said
he
expected
Muse's
seventh
album
to
be
released
in
early
2015,
saying:
&quot;The
last
two
albums,
we
sort
of
veered
away
from
our
instruments
a
little
bit.
We
sort
of
focused
on
things
like
synthesisers,
drum
machines
and
various
electronics
and
stuff.
I
kind
of
feel
like
on
this
next
album,
weâ€™re
going
to
veer
back
towards
musicianship
again
and
focusing
on
our
own
instruments:
guitar,
bass
and
drums.
Itâ€™s
probably
going
to
be
a
bit
of
a
rawer
album,
and
definitely
a
bit
more
rock,
Iâ€™d
say.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-112"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bellamy
also
mentioned
the
possibility
of
a
<a
href="/wiki/Concept_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concept
album">concept
album</a>
and
a
non-conventional
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-113"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Muse
are
an
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>
band
and
are
often
associated
with
<a
href="/wiki/Space_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Space
rock">space
rock</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Progressive_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Progressive
rock">progressive
rock</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
music
currently
mixes
sounds
from
genres
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electronic
dance
music">electronic
music</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Experimental_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Experimental
rock">experimental
rock</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Classical_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classical
music">classical
music</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_opera?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
opera">rock
opera</a>
and
many
others.<sup
id="cite_ref-rocksound_114-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rocksound-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
was
described
as
a
&quot;trashy
three-piece&quot;
by
Matthew
Bellamy
on
the
BBC
during
2002.<sup
id="cite_ref-Muse_interview_on_BBC_2002_115-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Muse_interview_on_BBC_2002-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
the
band's
association
with
progressive
rock,
Dominic
Howard
has
said:
&quot;I
associate
it
[progressive
rock]
with
10-minute
guitar
solos,
but
I
guess
we
kind
of
come
into
the
category.
A
lot
of
bands
are
quite
ambitious
with
their
music,
mixing
lots
of
different
styles
â€“
and
when
I
see
that
I
think
it's
great.
I've
noticed
that
kind
of
thing
becoming
a
bit
more
mainstream.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-116"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Stylistic_changes">Stylistic
changes</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Stylistic
changes">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>For
their
second
<i><a
href="/wiki/Origin_of_Symmetry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Origin
of
Symmetry">Origin
of
Symmetry</a></i>
(2001)
album,
the
band
wanted
to
enhance
their
sound
into
a
more
progressive,
confident
and
aggressive
sound:
&quot;Looking
back,
(Chris
regarding
to
the
sound
of
their
previous
album)
there
isn't
much
difference
sonically
between
the
mellow
stuff
and
the
heavier
tracks.
The
heavy
stuff
really
could
have
been
a
lot
heavier
and
that's
what
we
want
to
do
with
this
album.&quot;
<sup
id="cite_ref-117"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
third
release,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Absolution_(Muse_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolution
(Muse
album)"
class="mw-redirect">Absolution</a></i>
(2003),
followed
its
predecessor's
tendency,
increasing
the
band's
heaviness
and
intensity
alongside
its
ambitious
thematics.
The
album
also
features
songs
with
prominent
string
arrangements
and
starts
to
draw
influences
from
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Black_Holes_and_Revelations?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Holes
and
Revelations">Black
Holes
and
Revelations</a></i>
(2006)
is
a
more
<a
href="/wiki/Electronica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electronica">electronica</a>
â€“
and
<a
href="/wiki/Space_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Space
rock">space
rock</a>
â€“
oriented
album,
though
some
tracks
keep
the
heaviness
of
the
band's
previous
work,
while
others
show
a
more
melodic
style,
akin
to
the
musical
style
of
their
first
album,
<i>Showbiz</i>
(1999).
<i>Black
Holes
and
Revelations</i>
was
influenced
by
artists
like
<a
href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Depeche
Mode">Depeche
Mode</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Lightning_Bolt_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lightning
Bolt
(band)">Lightning
Bolt</a>,
as
well
by
various
styles
of
Asian
and
European
music,
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Naples?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Naples">Naples
music</a>;
additionally,
the
band
listened
to
radio
stations
from
the
Middle
East
during
the
album's
recording
sessions.<sup
id="cite_ref-119"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Muse's
fifth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
(album)">The
Resistance</a></i>
(2009)
is
centred
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Symphonic_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Symphonic
rock">symphonic
rock</a>
and
progressive
rock
genres,
as
demonstrated
in
the
tracks
&quot;Resistance&quot;
and
the
&quot;Exogenesis:
Symphony&quot;.
Although
in
places
it
is
sonically
softer
than
its
predecessors,
it
still
contains
a
number
of
'heavy'
compositions.
The
album
is
heavily
influenced
by
classical
music
as
well
as
rock
acts
such
as
Queen,
<a
href="/wiki/Ultravox?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ultravox">Ultravox</a>
(&quot;Guiding
Light&quot;
features
a
heavy
&quot;Vienna&quot;
influence)
and
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>.
Queen's
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_May?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
May">Brian
May</a>
has
praised
Muse's
work,
calling
the
band
&quot;extraordinary
musicians&quot;,
who
&quot;let
their
madness
show
through,
always
a
good
thing
in
an
artist.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_120-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Muse's
sixth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_2nd_Law?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
2nd
Law">The
2nd
Law</a></i>
(2012)
has
a
much
broader
range
of
influences,
ranging
from
<a
href="/wiki/Funk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Funk">funk</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Film_scores?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Film
scores"
class="mw-redirect">film
scores</a>
to
<a
href="/wiki/Electronica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electronica">electronica</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Dubstep?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dubstep">dubstep</a>.
<i>The
2nd
Law</i>
is
influenced
by
rock
acts
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
(on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Supremacy_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supremacy
(song)">Supremacy</a>&quot;)
as
well
as
<a
href="/wiki/Dubstep?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dubstep">dubstep</a>
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Skrillex?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skrillex">Skrillex</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nero_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nero
(band)">Nero</a>
(on
&quot;The
2nd
Law:
Unsustainable&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-121"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Follow_Me_(Muse_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Follow
Me
(Muse
song)">Follow
Me</a>&quot;,
with
the
latter
being
co-produced
by
Nero),
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Jackson">Michael
Jackson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stevie
Wonder">Stevie
Wonder</a>
(on
&quot;Panic
Station&quot;
which
features
musicians
who
performed
on
Stevie
Wonder's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Superstition_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Superstition
(song)">Superstition</a>&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-122"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup>)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hans
Zimmer">Hans
Zimmer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-123"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup>
Additionally,
the
album
marks
the
first
performance
of
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Wolstenholme?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Wolstenholme"
class="mw-redirect">Chris
Wolstenholme</a>
on
lead
vocals,
who
wrote
two
songs
for
the
album
about
his
battle
with
alcoholism
â€“
&quot;Save
Me&quot;
and
&quot;Liquid
State&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-124"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Critics
have
made
comparisons
between
Muse's
early
work
with
the
one
from
the
English
alternative
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>,
with
criticism
directed
towards
Bellamy's
vocal
style.
Additionally,
in
a
1999
issue
of
the
French
magazine
<i>Rock
Sound</i>,
Bellamy
named
<i>The
Bends</i>
by
Radiohead
and
Nirvana's
<i>Nevermind</i>
as
the
most
important
albums
of
the
decade.<sup
id="cite_ref-125"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-126"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup>
However
since
then
the
band
have
clarified
these
statements
various
times<sup
id="cite_ref-127"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
have
stated,
that
what
they
meant
to
say
was,
that
Nirvana
and
Radiohead
were
the
most
successful
alternative
rock
bands
in
the
1990s,
and
were
influential
to
many
bands,
but
that
does
not
necessarily
mean
that
Radiohead
was
an
influence
for
them.
On
the
other
hand,
Muse
acknowledges
Nirvana
as
a
major
influence.<sup
id="cite_ref-128"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bellamy
has
stated
various
times
that
Radiohead
&quot;really
don't
do
much
for
[him]&quot;
and
attributes
the
similarities
to
the
fact
that
both
bands
are
notably
influenced
by
the
alternative
rock
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Buckley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Buckley">Jeff
Buckley</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-musewiki.org_129-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-musewiki.org-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_approaches">Musical
approaches</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
approaches">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Many
Muse
songs
are
recognisable
by
lead
vocalist
Matthew
Bellamy's
use
of
<a
href="/wiki/Vibrato?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vibrato">vibrato</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Falsetto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Falsetto">falsetto</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Melisma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melisma">melismatic
phrasing</a>,
influenced
primarily
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Buckley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Buckley">Jeff
Buckley</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-musewiki.org_129-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-musewiki.org-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
pianist,
Matt
Bellamy
often
utilises
the
broken
chords
technique
(<a
href="/wiki/Arpeggio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arpeggio">arpeggio</a>)
on
several
piano-based
songs.
Some
influences
in
Bellamy's
playing
include
late
<a
href="/wiki/Classical_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classical
music">classical</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Romanticism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Romanticism">Romantic
era</a>
composers
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Sergei_Rachmaninov?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sergei
Rachmaninov"
class="mw-redirect">Sergei
Rachmaninov</a>
(in
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Butterflies_and_Hurricanes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butterflies
and
Hurricanes">Butterflies
and
Hurricanes</a>&quot;),
<a
href="/wiki/Pyotr_Tchaikovsky?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pyotr
Tchaikovsky"
class="mw-redirect">Pyotr
Tchaikovsky</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hector_Berlioz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hector
Berlioz">Hector
Berlioz</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ludwig
van
Beethoven">Ludwig
van
Beethoven</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franz
Liszt">Franz
Liszt</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Camille_Saint-Sa%C3%ABns?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Camille
Saint-Sa&euml;ns">Camille
Saint-Sa&euml;ns</a>
(in
&quot;I
Belong
to
You
(Mon
Coeur
S'ouvre
&Agrave;
Ta
Voix)&quot;),
and
<a
href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fr&eacute;d&eacute;ric
Chopin">Fr&eacute;d&eacute;ric
Chopin</a>
(in
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/United_States_of_Eurasia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States
of
Eurasia">United
States
of
Eurasia</a>&quot;)
among
others.
He
also
draws
influence
from
more
contemporary
composers,
namely
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Reich?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Reich">Steve
Reich</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Philip_Glass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Philip
Glass">Philip
Glass</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-130"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
several
Muse
songs
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bass_line?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bass
line"
class="mw-redirect">bass
line</a>
is
used
as
the
central
motif,
often
with
the
guitar
providing
an
extra
layer
to
the
song.
The
bass
line
adds
embellishments
in
the
lower
register.
The
bass
usually
is
<a
href="/wiki/Fuzz_bass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fuzz
bass">fuzz
bass</a>,
an
overdriven,
distorted
tone.
Other
electronic
effects
are
also
applied
to
the
bass
tone
to
achieve
a
greater
weight
and
depth.
This
allows
the
bass
guitar
to
serve
as
counterfoil
to
the
main
chord
progression,
often
playing
higher
notes,
or
electronic
sounds.
Both
bass
and
guitar
also
play
unison
parts
on
occasion,
adding
emphasis
to
specific
melodies
and
riffs
(see
&quot;Hysteria&quot;
post-second
chorus;
&quot;Dead
Star&quot;
main
riff).
Both
Matt
and
Chris
use
touch
screen
controllers,
often
built
into
their
instruments;
this
touch
screen
can
control
a
variety
of
synthesisers
and
digital
effects
pedals
but
is
most
often
used
with
a
Korg
Kaoss
pad
and/or
a
Digitech
Whammy
pedal.<sup
id="cite_ref-131"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>As
a
guitarist,
Bellamy
often
utilises
<a
href="/wiki/Arpeggiator?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arpeggiator"
class="mw-redirect">arpeggiator</a>
and
Pitch-shift
effects
to
create
a
more
&quot;electronic&quot;
sound,
citing
<a
href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimi
Hendrix">Jimi
Hendrix</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Morello?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Morello">Tom
Morello</a>
as
influences
for
this
method.<sup
id="cite_ref-bellamy_22-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bellamy-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
contrast,
his
guitar
playing
is
also
influenced
by
a
more
classical
harmonic
aesthetic,
particularly
the
style
of
<a
href="/wiki/Latin_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latin
music"
class="mw-redirect">Latin</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Music_of_spain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
of
spain"
class="mw-redirect">Spanish
guitar</a>
music,
as
Matt
Bellamy
cites:
&quot;I
learnt
some
Spanish
guitar
music
that
opened
up
a
world
of
different
harmonies
and
making
music
and
a
different
sort
of
passion,
very
heavy
music
but
it
hasn't
got
a
distortion
pedal.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-132"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Lyrical">Lyrical</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Lyrical">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Most
earlier
Muse
songs
lyrically
dealt
with
introspective
themes,
including
relationships,
social
alienation,
and
difficulties
they
had
encountered
while
trying
to
establish
themselves
in
their
hometown.
However,
with
the
band's
progress,
their
song
concepts
have
become
more
ambitious,
addressing
issues
such
as
the
fear
of
the
evolution
of
technology
in
their
<i>Origin
of
Symmetry</i>
(2001)
album.
They
deal
mainly
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Apocalypse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apocalypse">apocalypse</a>
in
<i>Absolution</i>
(2003)
and
with
catastrophic
war
in
<i>Black
Holes
and
Revelations</i>
(2006).
<i>The
Resistance</i>
(2009)
was
a
concept
album
based
around
the
plot
and
themes
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nineteen
Eighty-Four">Nineteen
Eighty-Four</a></i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/George_Orwell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Orwell">George
Orwell</a>.
Their
latest
album,
<i>The
2nd
Law</i>
(2012)
relates
to
economics,
thermodynamics,
and
apocalyptic
themes.</p>








<p>Books
that
have
influenced
Muse's
lyrical
themes
include:</p>








<ul>









<li><i><a
href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nineteen
Eighty-Four">Nineteen
Eighty-Four</a></i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/George_Orwell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Orwell">George
Orwell</a>,<sup

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Concert_tours">Concert
tours</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Muse_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit

function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Muse_%28band%29&page=1&ac=24&qid=3371E1160E30AC354043092EFF6D9EAD&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

<script
type="text/javascript">








var
ask
=
ask
||
{};









(function(){












var
_timedOut
=
false,
















_fullPayload
=
window.backfillParam
||
{},
















_timeFromSerpStart
=
null,
































_adsLoggingTimeout
=
null,
















_dynamicLoggingTimeout
=
null;



























try{
















_timeFromSerpStart
=
((new
Date()
-

-

_adsLoggingTimeout
=

-

_dynamicLoggingTimeout
=
Math.max(_adsLoggingTimeout,
1);












}catch(e){
































_dynamicLoggingTimeout
=
2000;












}













function
mixinCSAAdData(payload){
















var
externalData
=
{




















csaInfo:
{
















































domTime:
ask.CSA.domReadyTime
?
ask.CSA.domReadyTime
:

?

:
0,

?
ask.CSA.adsShownTime
:
0,

ask.CSA.serpShownTime
?
ask.CSA.serpShownTime
:
0,
















































supplement:
_timedOut,
















































serpTimedOut:
!!ask.CSA.showSerpTimeoutFired,
















































serpTimeoutStartTime:
ask.CSA.showSerpStartTime
?
ask.CSA.showSerpStartTime
:
0,
















































dynamicTimeout:
_dynamicLoggingTimeout




















}
















};
















payload.pl_time
=
ask.CSA.responseTime
?
ask.CSA.responseTime
:
0;
















payload.pl_tnum
=
ask.CSA.numTopAds
?
ask.CSA.numTopAds
:
0;
















payload.pl_bnum
=
ask.CSA.numBottomAds
?
ask.CSA.numBottomAds
:
0;
















payload.pl_rnum
=
parseInt(payload.pl_tnum)
+
parseInt(payload.pl_bnum);
















try{




















payload.pl_edata
=
JSON.stringify(externalData);
















}catch(e){




































}












}














if
(ask
&&
ask.CSA)
{
















ask.CSA.addCSALoadCallback(function(){

=
_timedOut
?
{
pl_supplement:
true
}
:
_fullPayload;





















mixinCSAAdData(payload);





















logBackfillEvent(payload);
















},
function(){








































_timedOut
=
true;





















logBackfillEvent(_fullPayload);
















},
_dynamicLoggingTimeout);












}
else
{
















logBackfillEvent(_fullPayload);
